Taicang Domestically Produced Goods Exhibition Discovers Japanese Goods The Shanghai Domestically Produced Goods Touring Group came to Taicang on the 5th of this month and jointly held a Domestically Produced Goods Exhibition with the county party headquarters and the First People's Education Center in the Sanyiguo Shame Museum in the city starting on the 6th. Under the name of the Domestically Produced Goods Exhibition, it was actually a temporary marketplace. At about 9 a.m. on the 8th, Lu Zuoheng and Zhang Menghua and other citizens of the city went to visit. They suddenly saw printed muslin cloth and twill flannel cloth and other goods displayed there, and were suspicious. It was difficult to determine whether they were domestically produced goods. Lu and others were moved by patriotic enthusiasm, and immediately prepared to buy a few feet to study and carefully examine the materials, which seemed suspicious. Because the matter concerned the promotion of domestically produced goods, they immediately prepared the procedures and asked the county party headquarters for investigation. After learning the situation, the county party headquarters immediately held a committee meeting and recommended Committee Member Yuan Kejian to send the cloth samples to the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters with official documents to ask the Enemy Goods Inspection Committee for identification. As a result, one section was indeed Japanese goods, and a certificate was immediately issued to confirm it. Now, Committee Member Yuan returned to Taicang on the afternoon of the 13th to report the process of going to Shanghai to all sectors of society.

Jiaxing Cracking Down on Red Pill Trafficking Organizations

The popularity of red pills is increasing in Jiaxing. The County Public Security Bureau is paying close attention to this and has ordered the police to investigate and crack down on them. In the past four or five days, several cases of red pill trafficking organizations have been cracked. Yesterday, the red pill trafficking organization of Lu Guibiao's family at No. 5 Fanhu Lake was cracked and many certificates were seized. The suspects were immediately sent to the court for interrogation, and Lu's residence was sealed.

Jiading Prohibition of Lantern Parades Leads to a Market Strike The lantern parades in various townships of the county have been repeatedly prohibited without success, and well-intentioned people in the city also initiated performances on the evening of the 12th. The next morning, the Anfen Bureau detained Chen Xingquan and two other leaders. In the evening, many people still gathered at the City God Temple with lanterns to continue the performances. Liu Rongxiang, the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau, and Gao Baozhen, the captain of the police team, went to persuade them, but to no avail. They set off on a parade to Guanjiaqiao, where they were stopped by the police team, who tore up the lanterns, seized the gongs and drums, and detained two people. The crowd followed to the county office. The police team prevented them from entering and confronted them at the gate. Captain Gao then climbed up and persuaded them to disperse and promised to release the detained people and return the gongs and drums. Unexpectedly, the crowd not only did not disperse but rushed forward and pushed Gao down. The police team also fought back. For a while, the order was chaotic. The police team fired a shot into the sky, and the crowd dispersed. As a result, more than a dozen public security bureau policemen including Cheng Changqing and Qin Wenli, and police team members Chen Debiao, Chen Zhaozhong, Lu Yongxi, and Zhu Hongsheng were injured. More than ten rioters and spectators were also injured. On the morning of the 14th, nine out of ten stores in the city went on strike. The county government convened an emergency meeting of the county chamber of commerce, various trade associations, and other organizations and groups, and decided to recommend Huang Shizuo, the head of the first district, to represent County Chief Xu, together with Tang Yiyu, a member of the standing committee of the county party headquarters, and Chen Peiqing, chairman of the county chamber of commerce, to persuade the merchants to open the market and release all the detained people. A disturbance finally subsided. Wuxi Teasing a Girl Leads to Murder

A Rong, the second daughter of Wang Erquan, a resident of Tianduoli Township, Northwest Tangtian, Fifth District (Tianshang City), is 14 years old and is simply dressed. She is engaged to the son of Liu Moubao nearby but has not yet married. You Xiajinjin, a villager, is about 30 years old and fond of women. Seeing A Rong's charming appearance, he followed her when she went out and teased her in every possible way. A Rong, who was humiliated for no reason, scolded You Xiajinjin severely. You Xiajin, ashamed and angry, kicked A Rong twice, hitting a vital part, and she died immediately. Seeing that he had caused trouble, A Jin asked Zhang Rongbao, the head of the village, to bribe the victim's family with 80 yuan to make peace. The head of the district, Tu Keqiang, has sent people to investigate the truth because the case involves human life, so as to report to the county for investigation.

Eating Large Shrimp Causes Death by Poisoning 78

Zhou Sanguan, a villager from Dazhuangli near Shuangheshang, Third Village, Tenth District of the county, is 18 years old and works as a farmer. At 9:00 a.m. on the 10th of this month, he went to the small river behind the village with a small fishing net to catch fish, and caught a large shrimp, about two inches long. Zhou Sanguan found the shrimp plump and lovely, so he put it in his mouth. Unexpectedly, the shrimp's large foot clamped his upper lip, causing him pain in his heart and lungs. Zhou Sanguan was extremely angry and removed the shrimp shell and swallowed the shrimp meat. But he was unable to speak. When he returned home for lunch, his upper lip suddenly swelled up and he felt unbearable pain. Because he was unable to seek medical treatment, he died last night.

Changzhou Police Officer Commits Suicide with a Gun

The first squad of the twentieth police team stationed in Wuyi Xiaoxinqiao Town had a police officer named Fang Chengjin, who was about thirty years old. On the night of the 12th, he was dispatched to stand guard as usual. Fang said that he was sick and could not go. At about 10:00 p.m., he suddenly went out again. Unexpectedly, when Fang walked to the drill ground next to the team headquarters, the guard suddenly heard a bang. He rushed to check and saw Fang had been shot in the head and fell to the ground and died. It was found that he had committed suicide with a box gun. The police team leader Mao Gangsheng reported to the county court. On the 13th, the inspecting prosecutor went to the countryside to inspect and confirmed that he had committed suicide by shooting himself.

Zhenjiang Health Campaign Exhibition Opens

The Provincial Capital Health Campaign Exhibition, prepared by the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau together with various agencies, has been receiving health exhibits collected from various parties in succession, so the association has been extremely busy arranging the venue these days. It is reported that there are no less than a thousand exhibits in this exhibition. Among them, the difficult childbirth pictures of women from the midwifery school attached to the provincial hospital and the shape of the fetus from one month to October treated with medicine in the provincial hospital are the most valuable. The hospital sent many female nurses from the department to the venue yesterday morning to make the layout suitable. The representative of the Ministry of Interior's Health Department also arrived in Zhenjiang last night and brought a large number of exhibits. It is scheduled to hold the opening ceremony of the Health Campaign Congress in the county public sports ground at 9:00 a.m. (15th) and parade throughout the city during the meeting.

Yangzhou Canal Water Rises Sharply, Canal Banks in Danger

The water level in the Grand Canal in Jiangbei has risen sharply recently without receding. The water level gauge at the Sanyugou Sluice in Jiangdu reached one foot and one foot and four inches yesterday, which is more than one foot and four inches higher than the highest water level last year. It is also reported that the spring repair project of the canal has not been completed due to lack of funds, which is quite worrying. After repeated consultations with the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society by the Canal Engineering Bureau, it was approved to allocate 126,000 yuan for the project. However, the amount is still insufficient. Xu Dingkang, the director of the Canal Engineering Bureau, submitted a revised estimate of this year's spring repair to the province in April of this year, requesting Chairman Gu to allocate funds to start construction. Two months have passed since then, and no order has been received to comply. The water level of the canal is increasing day by day, and the future is worrying. As for the west bank stone work, construction has been underway for nearly two months, and only more than 90,000 yuan of the project funds have been allocated from the county's land donation to the Finance Department. Recently, stone merchants have been demanding payment one after another. Director Xu feels deeply that the economy is not enough, but the important projects cannot be ignored. Yesterday, he sent a telegram to Chairman Gu requesting help.

Mud Digger Dies in the Mud 79

Liu Wanqi, 29 years old, lives behind Jian Dao Lane, east of Zhunti Temple, Dongguan Street in this city. Liu has been making a living by digging and selling loess for a living. Liu took several people to Huangni Mountain outside Bianyimen this (13th) morning to dig mud. Because the excavated area was too deep, the upper loess suddenly collapsed, burying Liu in the soil in an instant. After being rescued from the soil by the people who went with him, he had already lost his breath and died. It is also tragic.

Rugao Oppression of Workers Leads to Turmoil 81

The Li Fort area of this county is recruiting workers to dredge the Chuanzhang River. The Ding Suo Town section has already started construction. Unexpectedly, on the third afternoon of the start of construction, a huge turmoil occurred. At that time, three or five workers were resting because they were hungry. The supervisor (the instructor of the security team in the area) Xiang Bin saw this and whipped them severely with a horse whip, forcing them to work. As a result, hundreds of workers were furious and stopped working together. They rushed to beat Xiang. Seeing that the situation was not good, Xiang fled back to the team headquarters. At that time, thousands of workers, like a tide, went ashore to chase and surround the district team headquarters, cursing loudly, unanimously demanding that Xiang be dismissed immediately. The town chief Qiu reported to the district chief Chen by phone. Chen rushed to the scene after hearing the news. His poor handling of the situation further angered the workers, who picked up bricks and tiles and threw them at Chen. Chen fled with his head in his hands. Later, after Town Chief Qiu persuaded them with kind words and promised to submit a request to dismiss Xiang, the workers calmed down and dispersed.

Xiaoshan Fishermen Strive for Baima Lake 82

Baima Lake in Xixiang, Xiaoshan, covers an area of more than ten miles and has always been a place for thousands of farmers in Xixiang to fish. Unexpectedly, recently Dong Xiaohou and other gentry from Nanxiang submitted a request to Zhejiang University to take over the lake as an official property, build dams to raise fish, and prohibit fishermen from fishing, resulting in the severance of the livelihoods of thousands of fishing households. Yesterday, they sent a telegram to the provincial and county authorities, striving to recover the inherent people's property. The county government has convened a meeting of residents along the lake to discuss the matter, and a telegram has been sent to the Provincial Department of Construction to request instructions. In addition, more than ten representatives from the fishing households have gone to the province to petition.

Local News

Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement Expires 83

Today it expires naturally, and new tariffs will be levied from tomorrow.

The Sino-Japanese Tariff Reciprocity Agreement expires on May 15 (today). Our government authorities have repeatedly stated that the agreement will expire naturally and there is no doubt about it. Now the customs authorities have received an order from the Ministry of Finance to levy new tariffs on Japanese goods starting tomorrow (16). The details are as follows:

Reasons for the Agreement From the late Qing Dynasty to the Beiyang government era, China's tariff rights were lost and controlled by foreigners, resulting in low tariff rates on foreign goods, which allowed them to be sold to China as much as possible. The wealth of the Chinese people has been exploited by foreigners for decades, resulting in a weakening of national power and a decline in people's strength. After the National Government established Nanjing, it began negotiations to recover tariff autonomy. All countries had no objection, but Japan insisted on exchange conditions, so the Sino-Japanese Tariff Reciprocity Agreement was established, which still allowed Japan to maintain the right to sell Japanese goods at low tariffs. However, the period was set for three years, which will expire on May 15 this year. Our government temporarily signed the agreement because its primary goal was to recover tariff autonomy.

Expiration and Termination The agreement will expire today (May 15). All sectors of the public, groups, and domestic goods and industrial and commercial circles have long telegraphed not to renew the agreement, and our government has also decided to let it expire naturally and no longer negotiate. The Japanese side initially intended to continue negotiations with our country in order to extend the term in order to continue to sell Japanese goods. Japanese merchants and residents in this port held a meeting a month ago to request their government to contact us in an attempt to prolong it. However, because the treaty stated that it was impossible to continue and our country's attitude was extremely firm, they had to let it expire naturally and become invalid. Japanese goods were rushed Japanese people, in view of the fact that our country has no intention of continuing this agreement, have tried their best to rush Japanese goods to China before May 15, to sell them in the market, in order to collect the last gamble. Therefore, the number of Japanese goods transported to China in the past two months is really amazing. The reason is that half of them are for price reduction and dumping due to our resistance, and half of them are because the reciprocity agreement is about to expire, so they have to rush to ship them to China to avoid being levied new tariffs. New tariffs will be levied Since the government decided to let the agreement expire, the Ministry of Finance has instructed the customs and tax authorities to levy import tariffs on Japanese goods according to the new tariff regulations issued on January 1, 1931, starting on May 16 (tomorrow). The new tariffs levied on Japanese goods include cloth, seafood, fish and shellfish, totaling more than forty kinds. It is said that both customs and flood control surcharges will be levied at the same time.

Huang Fu, Chairman of the Administrative Yuan's Political Consolidation Committee in Ping, has been in Shanghai for days, contacting all parties. Zhu Shaoliang Talks About Governing Gansu 85

Facilitate transportation, improve agriculture, and other things must be determined after taking office. Zhu is scheduled to go west to take office this month.

Zhu Shaoliang, the newly appointed Chairman of the Gansu Provincial Government, flew from Beijing to Shanghai the day before yesterday and is scheduled to go to Gansu to take office this month. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Zhu at his residence yesterday and asked him about the current situation of Gansu and the policies for governing Gansu. Zhu gave a detailed reply as follows:

Current Situation of Gansu The reporter first asked Chairman Zhu about the current situation of Gansu. Zhu replied that he had not been there before, so he did not know the political and social realities. However, he had met with the former Chairman Shao Lizi in Beijing and learned about the situation there. The land is rich in resources, but most of them have not been developed. The people are mostly engaged in agriculture and animal husbandry. Therefore, the annual output of wool and animal skins, in addition to industrial raw materials such as cotton, is also very large. However, due to inconvenient transportation and high freight rates, it is declining day by day. Moreover, this year's drought has caused a disaster and the output of farmland has been sharply reduced, which has also reduced revenue. Therefore, the financial situation is very difficult, but it is still able to balance income and expenditure and maintain the status quo. The transportation in Gansu is very inconvenient. The only trunk road is the automobile road from Xi'an to Lanzhou, which is 1,100 miles long. It was built by the military and only leveled the roadbed. There is no scale of a highway. When Chairman Shao was in power, he planned to build and repave the road surface, which could be completed in about six or seven months.

Developing the Northwest Zhu continued to tell the reporter that the central government now attaches great importance to the development of the Northwest, and the people are also very interested in it. However, to seek development, it is necessary to open up roads and facilitate transportation first. All construction must have new machinery. Without convenient means of transportation, it is impossible to import a large amount of machinery. The central government has sent experts to investigate and plan for the improvement of agriculture. Moreover, several irrigation engines were imported during the drought years ago, but they could not be fully adopted due to financial resources and transportation. To seek the development of agriculture, reclamation and afforestation are also important facilities. The reporter then asked whether Chairman Shao had invited financial giants in Shanghai to discuss investment and development in the Northwest. Will there be further contact? Zhu replied that if transportation in Gansu can be improved, all parties will be happy to go there for development without the need for contact. Therefore, the most important thing for development is transportation.

Policy Guidelines The reporter then asked Zhu to announce his policy guidelines for governing Gansu. Zhu said that he could not talk about the so-called policy guidelines before he arrived in Gansu. The policy guidelines cannot be separated from the society and empty talk. It must be determined according to the situation of the society. I am not very familiar with the situation in Gansu at present, so I have not made any decisions on the policy guidelines. As for the candidates for the heads of various departments of the Gansu Provincial Government, they will remain the same and there will be no changes.

Going to Gansu This Month Zhu came to Shanghai this time to take care of personal matters. It is said that he will return to Beijing within this week for consultations. He will also go to Jiangxi to visit Chairman Chiang. He should be able to go to Gansu to take office this month.

Reduce Silk and Tea Freight Rates The Ministry of Communications Orders China Merchants Bureau 86

In order to reduce the freight rates of silk, tea, porcelain, lacquer, and tung oil, the Ministry of Communications yesterday issued an order to the China Merchants Bureau, saying that in order to implement the order, it was found that the Shanghai Local Association requested a reduction in the freight rates of silk, tea, porcelain, lacquer, and tung oil. The bureau previously submitted a reply requesting that silk, tea, and other trade associations sign special transportation contracts. The ministry has forwarded the matter to the Ministry of Industry for investigation. Now, the Ministry of Industry has sent a consultation stating that the bureau's proposal to sign special transportation contracts with silk, tea, porcelain, and other trade associations, as long as the cost is not loss-making, should try its best to reduce freight rates to achieve a win-win situation, which is the key to maintaining domestic goods and developing shipping. However, the bureau has not stated to what extent the original fixed water freight rates for the above-mentioned goods can be reduced. Although the ministry has forwarded the order, it is feared that merchants are still waiting to see. If the bureau first checks the usual practice, determines a reduction method, and then the ministry forwards the order to the trade associations for compliance, it seems more practical. It is appropriate to consult and request investigation, implement the method, and reply. Do not delay this order.

Three Representatives of Overseas Chinese Expelled from Mexico and Staying in Shanghai Jointly Issue a Statement

Expressing Gratitude for Assistance and Renewing Appeals for Relief, Detailing the Reasons for Chinese Exclusion and the Suffering Endured 88

Over four thousand Chinese nationals who were expelled from Mexico and have returned to our country in succession. Currently remaining in Shanghai are the three representatives of the victims who returned the day before yesterday (the 12th), Mr. Huang Zhulin, Mr. Lin Wenli, and Mr. Lin Huiyao, who are carrying out various relief efforts in Shanghai. The following is a record of their joint statement issued yesterday:

Gratitude for Assistance: The refugee Chinese arrived in Shanghai on the President Hoover ship the day before yesterday (the 12th). They were met by Mr. Peng Canguang, the General Manager of the Shanghai Global Overseas Chinese General Association, who personally came to the ship to express his condolences and lead all the refugee Chinese ashore. In addition to providing meals and lodging, they were also given ten silver dollars per person. The Overseas Chinese General Association is not only capable of participating in practical work for overseas Chinese, but its key personnel also possess a spirit of dedication that is tireless day and night, which is truly admirable. On this occasion, Chairman Wu Chengyu of the association personally hosted the refugees, and Chairman Guo Shun personally went to the new customs wharf to supervise everything, which made the refugee Chinese feel very grateful. They all unanimously joined the association to show their sincere support. This time, they also received extensive publicity from the Shanghai press, which had a significant impact on the relief negotiations and benefited the future of the refugee Chinese in no small measure. In addition, they received 1,000 yuan donated by Mr. Wu Tiecheng, the Mayor of Shanghai and Honorary Chairman of the Overseas Chinese General Association, for relief purposes. Mayor Wu is truly the driving force behind this relief effort for the refugee Chinese. We, on behalf of all the refugee Chinese, express our sincere gratitude.

Purpose of Staying in Shanghai: Approximately four thousand Mexican refugee Chinese have already been deported back to China, and there are more than four times that number (approximately 20,000) who will continue to return to the country one after another. If no measures are taken to maintain them, how can their future be ensured? Therefore, the refugee Chinese have designated Shanghai as the economic and political center of our country and specially dispatched us (three representatives) to stay in Shanghai in order to carry out various necessary tasks under the leadership of the Global Overseas Chinese General Association, such as appealing for relief from all sectors and urging the government to negotiate. This is the purpose of our staying in Shanghai.

Establishing an Association to Maintain the Refugees: With so many refugees returning to the country at once, if a comprehensive relief plan is not devised in advance, these refugees will either become beggars or turn into bandits, which is extremely dangerous. Although the central government has been saying that it will find ways to provide relief, the Chinese exclusion in Mexico has a history of two years, and no practical measures have been seen. The government's neglect of the refugees is excessive; this is a factual representation and not a criticism of the government. We are also well aware that the government is in a difficult situation during this time of national crisis. What we hope from the government is that since there is no solution, we can only seek self-reliance by devising our own solutions and asking the government for help. This is a matter of vital interest to us, and it is imperative to establish an association for maintenance.

Requesting Relief: Overseas Chinese have always done their best to contribute to the revolutionary public welfare undertakings of the motherland, which is well known and need not be elaborated upon. This time, our overseas Chinese in Mexico have unfortunately suffered a major disaster, and their situation is extremely tragic. They have homes but cannot return. We can only appeal to the charitable people in the country and our compatriots in the concession to provide generous relief. We also hope that the important figures in the party and the country will remember their roots and provide material assistance to alleviate the suffering of tens of thousands of refugee Chinese in Mexico and provide them with effective follow-up measures. This will not only benefit the individual refugees themselves but will also be of considerable importance to the national honor.

Distant Causes of Chinese Exclusion: The Chinese exclusion in Mexico began on June 12, 1931. The most active initiator was Mr. Wan Nuoshi, a member of the Mexican Congress. Under the leadership of Mr. Wan, a group of unemployed hooligans and unemployed workers organized the Chinese Exclusion Party, with Mr. Wan concurrently serving as one of the chairmen of the party. In fact, the promotion of Chinese exclusion in Mexico this time contained economic and political factors. The Mexican government was the driving force behind the manipulation and planning of Chinese exclusion. In terms of economics, our overseas Chinese in Mexico did have a great influence in commerce and agriculture, which was not only envied by the Mexican government and people but also aroused the desire for competition and plunder among foreign residents in Mexico (such as the Japanese). At that time, Mexican intellectuals also suffered from increasing unemployment due to the global economic impact. In terms of politics, Mexican politics has always been complex. The central and local governments often have different opinions, and there are different opinions on Chinese exclusion and pro-Chinese sentiments. When the pro-Chinese faction is in power, the overseas Chinese in Mexico can live and work in peace. If the Chinese exclusion faction gains power, it will arbitrarily oppress, expel, and abuse them. Shanxi and Shaanxi provinces are important provinces in Mexico, where Chinese business and agriculture are concentrated. Whenever Chinese exclusion incidents occur, the overseas Chinese in Shanxi and Shaanxi provinces suffer the most. These two provinces are the source of Chinese exclusion. These are the distant causes of Chinese exclusion in Mexico.

Immediate Causes of Chinese Exclusion: Since Mexico launched Chinese exclusion, after a certain period of lessons, our government, in addition to adopting empty gestures of negotiation, has had no other effective measures, which has led to contempt from all levels of Mexican society. From contempt to arbitrary actions, from arbitrary actions to reckless abuse, the government advocates it, the people echo it, and thus a very orderly Chinese exclusion movement has evolved. Recently, because our country lost the Northeast, the Mexican government and people were even more contemptuous and became even more severe. On January 1st of this year, it happened to be the day when Mr. Manuel Paix of the Chinese Exclusion Party took office as the governor of Shanxi Province. As a result, the atmosphere of Chinese exclusion rose sharply, and the Chinese Exclusion Party went out to act wantonly. This is the immediate cause of Chinese exclusion in Mexico.

Suffering Greatly: Since the revival of Chinese exclusion, our overseas Chinese in Mexico have been unable to stand in Shanxi and Shaanxi provinces. The Mexican government is implementing the most stringent Chinese exclusion policy against Chinese Confucian scholars, especially imposing unprecedented harsh restrictions on Chinese businessmen. Every Chinese store must employ at least eight Mexican workers out of ten people. Not only that, but the business tax has been increased from ten yuan to one hundred yuan. Chinese businessmen certainly cannot accept this unreasonable harsh regulation. Our diplomatic authorities are limited in their power and cannot negotiate for cancellation, so they have no choice but to voluntarily auction off their existing goods at low prices. This loss is counted in the tens of millions. The Mexican government also instigated the Chinese Exclusion Party to rob the overseas Chinese of their property and certificates (i.e., residence permits). At the same time, the Mexican government issued an order under the pretext of protecting foreigners, uniformly inspecting the certificates, but unbeknownst to them, the Chinese certificates had already been robbed by the Chinese Exclusion Party. As a result, there was a panic of "illegal residence," and the police authorities in various places simultaneously ordered the arrest of Chinese without certificates. The overseas Chinese in Mexico suffered the loss of property and were illegally arrested and expelled, using such cruel methods to inflict tangible and intangible suffering on the overseas Chinese in Mexico.

Smuggling into the United States: Our overseas Chinese, witnessing the cruel methods of the Mexican government, fled their homes and smuggled into the United States to avoid danger. The United States government was also well aware of the plight of the overseas Chinese in Mexico who were forced to smuggle into the United States this time. It was still able to provide humanitarian assistance with travel expenses and send them back to China, for which we are very grateful. Upon returning to our country, the so-called largest metropolis of Shanghai, apart from the Overseas Chinese General Association launching relief efforts and Mayor Wu providing assistance, the rest of the government and various organizations are indifferent, which is truly regrettable. Now that the Overseas Chinese General Association has launched relief efforts and entrusted the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Bank (No. 9 Jiujiang Road) to handle the collection of funds, we hope that all sectors at home and abroad will generously contribute to this righteous cause in order to pool the strength of everyone and provide relief to these tens of thousands of innocent refugees. We, on behalf of the refugees, express our deep gratitude.

Reconstruction of the North Railway Station Commences 89

Formal Contract Signed Today

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration invited bids for the reconstruction of the destroyed site of the North Railway Station. The bid was opened on the first of this month and was won by the Zhongnan Construction Company. The construction cost is estimated at 50,146 yuan. The Administration has submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways to send personnel to Shanghai to jointly sign a contract with the company. It is now known that the original text of the contract was completed last Saturday and is scheduled to be formally signed today (Monday). As for the construction project, it has already begun to be constructed, and the old houses are currently being demolished. It is expected to be completed in three months. The building has two floors. The upper floor is used for the offices of the Traffic Department, and the lower floor is used as a ticket office and waiting room. Because it is a temporary nature (the station must be moved in the future), the rebuilt building is not very elaborate.

During This Time of Suppressing Bandits and Resisting Japan

Do Not Fall into the Trap of Internal Strife

According to Xinhua News Agency, Liu Wenhui and Deng Xihou of the Sichuan Army have recently started disputes again. Generals Liu Xiang, Liu Cunhou, Yang Sen, and others of the Sichuan Army, since Liu Wenhui's transfer, have disregarded national survival during this period of suppressing bandits and resisting Japan and have considered personal rights, which is extremely inappropriate. A separate telegram has been sent to Liu, ordering him to quickly return to his original defense area and stop the dispute to avoid delaying the overall situation, otherwise effective measures will be taken to stop it, etc."

Japanese Steamships Attempt to Fully Resume Navigation 91

Reducing Freight Rates to Compete with National Vessels, Plans to Increase Ships Between Hankou and Yichang

According to the Central News Agency, Japanese merchants have been encroaching on inland river navigation rights in our country for many years. However, since the outbreak of the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Shanghai War, the business of Japanese ships has plummeted, and many Japanese shipping companies have suspended operations. Now they are gradually recovering, but they have not yet returned to their original state. At present, Japanese merchants are planning to restore their original shipping services and add more ships. The following is an exploration of the situation:

Yangtze River Area: The Yangtze River route from Shanghai to Hankou has always been operated by ships from the China Merchants Bureau, Ning Shao Company, British Jardine Matheson Company, Taikoo Company, and Japanese Nisshin Company, totaling more than 70 ships, and Japanese ships accounted for the most, accounting for more than 40 ships. Since the outbreak of the Shenyang Incident and the Shanghai War, these more than 40 Japanese ships have had almost no passengers and no cargo, and they have been suspended for several months. As a result, the import of Japanese goods into the interior has almost disappeared. The Japanese government secretly subsidized the country's shipping companies, and later gradually resumed sailing, but has not yet returned to its original state. It is now known that Japanese shipping companies have decided to restore all of their ships to operation and plan to reduce freight rates in an attempt to seize all of the Yangtze River shipping, and there are also plans to increase the number of sailings on the Hankou-Yichang route.

South China Shipping: In the South China region, apart from a few mail ships operated by Nippon Yusen Kaisha, there is no Japanese shipping organization dedicated to operating in the South China region. Moreover, it is learned that the movement to boycott Japanese goods in Guangdong is very strong, so there are currently no plans to develop South China shipping.

Monopoly of North China: North China's shipping rights have long been seized by Japanese merchants. Japanese merchants have a considerable history of operating shipping in North China. At present, although some Chinese shipping companies can nominally compete with Japanese merchants on the North China route, according to shipping industry sources, some two shipping companies have Japanese shares secretly, which has aroused the attention of the Maritime Administration and will be investigated. According to Japanese shipping industry sources, the Japanese puppet government will add ships between Andong and Dalian so that goods from the three northeastern provinces can be transported to Dalian for transshipment and sale to various places.

National Traveler Sun Leshan's Letter Informs of the Situation in Jiangxi Province: Banditry Unsuppressed, Everything Abnormal 92

According to the Guowen News Agency, Sun Leshan, a national traveler from Anhui Province, has traveled upstream along the Yangtze River and has now reached Wuchang via Anhui and Jiangxi. Mr. Sun has sent a letter to the agency about the situation he observed along the way. The first letter is recorded as follows: "Jiangxi Province is rich in products, and those famous throughout the country include porcelain, summer cloth, Jiangxi wood, black tea, and paper. Today, due to the influence of soldiers and bandits, none of them have been revitalized, and the business markets have also declined. The current situation of each industry is recorded below for readers' information: Jingdezhen is the place of porcelain production, and its sales rank first in the country. In recent years, it has been ravaged by the Red bandits, and the porcelain workers have long been dispersed, and the industry has been stagnant. Compared with the past, it has fallen sharply. Later, the authorities made every effort to maintain the industry, and the banditry was slightly suppressed, and the porcelain workers also came to the town one after another to prepare to resume work. The kiln owners were also busy planning. Unexpectedly, the local banditry was slightly suppressed, and the situation in North China became tense. Since the loss of Rehe, the porcelain in the town has been greatly affected. Normally, millions of pieces are sold every year, and porcelain merchants from all over the country have special commissioners stationed in the town to purchase. This time, the Japanese pirates invaded Rehe, and the peace in Tianjin was shocked. Rumors abounded, and merchants held tight and advocated contraction, and telegraphed Jingdezhen to stop purchasing, which caused workers in various counties to become unemployed again. In previous years, the kilns were opened on March 1st, but this year they have not been opened on April 1st. More than 100,000 porcelain workers have no work to do. The summer cloth of Wanzai is favored by various provinces. Recently, due to the improvement of materials, ladies from all walks of life mostly use Indian silk and fine cloth instead of summer cloth. According to the Jiujiang Chamber of Commerce, recently, the summer cloth shipped to Shanghai has actually been returned in its original boxes, and the summer cloth is too narrow and the tailoring is too uneconomical. This is also a major reason for the failure. Wuning black tea has always been sold to Russia and has a considerable history in international trade. Since the severance of relations between China and Russia, tea farmers have not hired workers to pick tea because the price of tea is not enough to pay the tea pickers, so the tea leaves are mostly allowed to fall by themselves and are used as fuel. Although China and Russia have resumed relations recently, the banditry has not ended, and no one has continued to operate. Most of the wood used in the Gan River Basin, the Yangtze River Basin, and the Yellow River Basin comes from Gan County, Jiangxi. Gan County is famous throughout the country for its lush forests. Since 1928, Gan County has become a bandit area, and postal services have been cut off. The people of Gan County cannot go downstream smoothly, and timber merchants are helping the old and the young to escape. Although the forest is good, they cannot take care of it. It is sad to say that the sales volume of Nanchang paper in various provinces is also very considerable. In recent years, the handicrafts of our country have been suppressed by imported products and machine-made products. The price of domestic goods is too expensive and the thickness is uneven, resulting in more losses. Recently, the primary and secondary schools in Nanchang use Italian paper, which is newspaper paper. Because the education funds are difficult, they have to use cheap and good imported products. This is the recent overview of the five major products of Jiangxi. All industries in Nanchang market use radio calls, but the people's purchasing power is weak. General stores are desolate and deserted. Commerce is so declining, but the population has increased. According to the person in charge of the investigation, the population has suddenly increased by more than 100,000 in recent years. These 100,000 people are refugees from the disaster areas. From the reverse side, the population is dense, but in fact, most of them are unemployed and homeless. According to the recent survey by the Liguo Education Hall, there were 3,000 people in the Nanchang money industry, and 1,000 people have recently lost their jobs. There were more than 300 porcelain households, and recently they have been reduced to the outside households. More than 2,000 people in the foreign goods industry have lost their jobs. There were originally more than 3,000 rickshaws, and recently they have been reduced to less than 2,000. The paper industry had an operating revenue of 4 million in previous years, and recently it has been reduced to 1 million or less. As for the expenses of various agencies and schools in the province, they are paid at 80% or 70% across the board. During the national crisis, salaries are paid at 80%, and the people of this province cooperate in suppressing the Communist bandits, and then they are paid at 70%. In addition, there are salary arrears, and the lower-level staff are almost unemployed. The local authorities in various counties also need to assess the financial resources of the people and raise funds for suppressing the Communist bandits. The county magistrates are privately corrupt and abuse the villagers, and the villagers often report to the administrative inspector and the provincial authorities. There are many middle schools in Nanchang because of the increase in population. In addition to the provincial medical college, the engineering college, the agricultural college, the commercial college, the first middle school, the second middle school, the first vocational school, the second vocational school, the girls' middle school, and the girls' vocational school in the provincial capital, there are also more than ten private middle schools. Among them, except for a few schools with specialized skills, the remaining middle schools have become factories for manufacturing middle-level hooligans. The children in the bandit area often hear that their houses have been destroyed and their families have been killed. The schools are also often stationed by troops, and many of them have no intention of studying, and the school authorities are also inevitably negligent in their business."

Ministry of Transportation Sends Engineers to Europe to Inspect Wireless Communications Industries in Various Countries and to Intern at Marconi Company 95

The Ministry of Transportation's International Radio Station is building several 160-foot-high antenna iron towers in Zhenru, Liuhang, and other places in order to directly communicate with the United Kingdom and has ordered two sets of transceivers from the British Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company at a cost of more than 800,000 yuan in Chinese currency. The machines have been shipped to Shanghai in succession, and there are about 1,500 large and small components. Construction has begun, and it is expected to be completed in mid-October and can be reported in the spring of 1935. [Report on Tragic Disaster in Shaanxi] 100

The Shanghai Chinese Jisheng Association recently received a report from the Meixian Relief Branch in Shaanxi Province, stating in a most urgent message: "Meixian County has suffered from disasters since 1928, with five years of failed harvests. The situation in 1932 and 1933 is even worse than in 1929 and 1930. Initially, people could dismantle houses, sell firewood, and sell their wives and children. Later, even wives and children could not find buyers, and houses were empty. Land prices are only one dime per mu, attracting buyers from other counties. Daughters are sold for three yuan each and become ghosts in foreign lands. Starved corpses line the roads. Even office staff have sunken cheeks and hollow eyes, filling their bellies with vegetable soup, constantly worried about interruptions, let alone coarse rice. In Tianjiapo, Southeast Township, a family of four in Guo Zhenfen's family starved to death. The wife, Wu, even cut flesh from her own buttocks to eat. Some criticized her, but who could know the desperation of a woman driven to such extremes by starvation? We urgently request relief, either in the form of food or seeds. Life or death, flesh or bone, we eagerly await assistance." Furthermore, the Tongxiang Disaster Relief Committee in Quanyi County reported that the disaster situation in the county has worsened in recent years, with everyone running out of food and every household running out of supplies. The number of disaster victims who are on the brink of death and desperately need relief is estimated to be over 30,000. Deaths are increasing dramatically. In addition, various tragedies such as suicides by drowning and poisoning occur frequently. It is now the beginning of summer, the time to sow autumn crops. Disaster victims are struggling to survive and have no seeds or labor. Even with rainfall, there is no way to plant. If the land is left barren again, it will inevitably lead to a complete catastrophe. We urgently request assistance. In addition to the 6,000 yuan in transportation costs urgently needed for relief in Xi'an, which the association will remit in installments, the association has also allocated 1,000 yuan for transportation, and yesterday allocated another 1,500 yuan, all of which will be transferred to the Shaanxi branch through the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank. We have no funds to help with the other urgent disasters in other counties and can do nothing. We especially hope that compassionate and virtuous people at home and abroad will join hands in providing assistance."

Market Strike in Jiading County Due to Ban on Lantern Parades 104

Dozens of Police and Civilians Injured

According to the old custom in Jiading County, there would be lantern shows and dragon boat races around the time of the Dragon Boat Festival in the lunar calendar. This practice has been discontinued for many years. This year, someone suddenly initiated it again. Lantern shows have already been held outside the East Gate, Shagang Gate of the South Gate, the Western Gate, and Loutang of the North Gate. However, no events had been held in the city center. The day before yesterday (the 13th), someone was collecting stamps in various shops in the city to organize a lantern show. This was discovered by the captain of the county police, who arrested two people on the spot, leading to a clash between the police and the civilians. Dozens of people were injured on both sides, and yesterday, the entire city went on strike, escalating the unrest. The details are listed below:

Incident Details: At around 10 AM the day before yesterday, Chen Xingquan, Chen Delin, and others were collecting stamps from shops such as Ruidasheng, Hongyuanguan, Beiyongda, Pingminlej, Wufeng, Zhengtai, Dacheng Yong, Qiaoyongxing, Taihe, Zhou Yongrun, Tongtaichang, Runyuanguan, Longji, Yuelaixi, and Fengshentai to organize a lantern show. Gao Baozhen, the captain of the county police, led a patrol and arrested Chen Xingquan and Chen Delin, along with the booklets, and sent them to the county government. Xu Weizhen, the county magistrate, handed them over to the Public Security Bureau for detention. The booklets contained words such as "Celebrating Victory." In the afternoon, Magistrate Xu ordered the police to work with the Public Security Bureau to strengthen prevention. At around 6 PM, three to four hundred people gathered in the City God Temple outside the East Gate, demanding the release of Chen Xingquan and Chen Delin and insisting on holding a lantern show. The Public Security Bureau sent Chief Inspector Liu Rongxiang, leading several unarmed policemen, to persuade them, but they were unable to control the large crowd. Since the City God Temple was very close to the county government, the merchants and civilians stormed the entrance of the county government. Shouts and cries arose. The entire police force was dispatched to stop them, but to no avail. They fired several shots into the air, which only further incited the crowd. Both sides started fighting. The civilians threw bricks at the county government, resulting in many injuries on both sides. It is said that forty to fifty civilians were injured and went to Kunshan, Suzhou, Taicang, and other places for treatment.

Injury Investigation: A total of seven people were injured from the Public Security Bureau. Chen Changqing suffered a head injury, and Qin Wenli suffered a leg injury. The injuries of these two were the most serious and life-threatening. Five others suffered minor injuries. As for the civilians, it was impossible to find out at the moment. Several eyewitnesses were interviewed, and their testimonies are listed below: Shen Xingquan suffered severe injuries to his waist and back. Gu Er'er, the owner of a pastry shop, was reportedly eating dinner in the shop when he was driven out by the police and suffered injuries to his head, waist, abdomen, hands, shoulders, legs, etc. Gu's wife, Yang, was grazed by a bullet on her forehead. A shop assistant, Han Yongqi, was injured in the shoulder. Xu Adi was injured in the hand. Zhang Bao was injured in the head, waist, hands, chest, and abdomen. Shen Agui was injured in the head. Others either went to the hospital or received treatment at home, and it was impossible to find out at the moment. Market Strike: After the reporter learned about this yesterday morning, he drove to Zhabei at 9 AM and took the Shanghai-Taicang long-distance bus to Jiading. He arrived at Jiading Station at 10 AM and hired a rickshaw to enter the city. When he arrived at the county government, Magistrate Xu was convening a meeting with the county chamber of commerce and other organizations. He could not attend the meeting, so he was interviewed by a section chief, who confirmed the details, which were similar to the reporter's investigation. When he left, he saw many civilians still gathered at the entrance of the county government, and there were various opinions. More than a dozen policemen guarded the entrance with guns. He then went to various streets and alleys and saw that all the shops were on strike. Only a few food shops opened small doors or a side door to serve customers. There were no policemen on duty in the city, just like the lunar New Year's Day. He took a bus back to Shanghai at 3 PM.

Police Officer Wu Linqing Shoots a Madman 105

Wu Linqing has been detained

Dachunpu from Nanjing, 35 years old, lived in Zhoujin Pailou in the city and worked as a peddler. Because of his mental illness, he had a manic episode after drinking alcohol on the 12th of this month. He held a kitchen knife and ran wildly on the road, randomly slashing, injuring Lou Xinru, and then ran towards Xueyuan Road. Police officer Wu Linqing chased after him. The madman slashed the police officer's wrist with the knife. The police officer immediately opened fire and pursued him. According to the family of the deceased, the third shot hit the madman's abdomen. The madman was sent to Shanghai Hospital for treatment and died of his injuries the day before yesterday. Yesterday, the No. 2 Police Station of District 1 ordered Di Jia Zhang Fu to report to the court for an autopsy. After prosecutor Zhang and others arrived at the hospital and verified the details, they ordered the family to collect the body. His parents claimed that the police officer had acted recklessly and caused the death of an innocent person, and they requested redress. The official instructed them to submit the case to the police station for review and processing by the court. Police officer Wu Linqing has been detained by Police Chief Liu since the madman's death.

Brave Woman Captures Street Robber 106

Stolen Goods Recovered on the Spot

Shen Shen, the 47-year-old wife of Shen Jusheng, a local resident who lives at No. 7 Xuejiabang Road in Nanshi and is currently a member of the Dongjiadu Fire Brigade, was returning home from mass at the Dongjiadu Cathedral at 6:30 yesterday morning when she was suddenly robbed by a thief at the entrance of Tongtai Lane. The thief snatched the gold earring from Shen Shen's right ear. Her ear was torn and bleeding. Fortunately, a passing woman witnessed the tragedy and tightly held the thief. Police officer Yang Siling from the District 1 Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau arrived and arrested the thief, recovering the stolen goods. The thief confessed, "Zhao Fuyin, 34 years old, from Tongzhou, lives at the No. 16 Pu Wharf," admitting to the robbery. The construction of the dormitory next to the Zhoujiazui Police Station, the Chengdu Road Police Station, the Victoria Nursing Home, and the West China Boys' School on Yuyuan Road are all progressing. Among private constructions, 426 projects are currently underway, 227 building plans have been submitted, and 129 have been approved. A large number of houses have been evaluated as tax standards, totaling 72 cases. There were 3,422 house inspections. Road sweeping collected 2,398 tons of garbage and 2,214 tons of gutter waste. Over 940,000 gallons of water were used for watering the roads and over 3 million gallons of water were used for washing the roads. 3,741 tons of domestic waste were transported to fill low-lying areas, and 12,101 tons were transported by contractors by boat. A total of 8,308 tons of garbage were incinerated in two incinerators.

The Public Works Department employed an average of 410 foremen, 510 craftsmen, and 6,045 laborers this month.

Daylight Robbery of a Car Carrying Opium in Western Shanghai 108

Lei Zaixi, the police chief of the Hejiajiao Police Station of the No. 2 Branch of the No. 6 District of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, received a report yesterday afternoon at 4 PM from Zhong Yuehua from Fujian and Xue Zhiming from Chongming, stating that they had taken a Yinghai Motor Company car, license number 571 and rental license number 12197, from the Old North Gate Minquan Road to Zhenru. Xue Zhiming was driving. Because there were two leather boxes of opium in the car, they took the route from Xieqiao in Nanshi to Tushanwan, turning into Zhongshan Road to reach Zhenru. When the car reached the intersection of Zhongshan Road and Daxi Road, seven robbers suddenly jumped out of the roadside, each holding a handgun, and blocked their path. They forcibly dragged them and the driver Xue Zhiming from the car. Another robber drove the car away towards the north. The opium belonged to the owner of the Tongchunhua Opium Company, entrusted to them to transport. Each box contained eight packages, and each package contained 150 taels, totaling approximately 6,000 yuan. Police Chief Lei immediately sent police to pursue the robbers, but they had already gone far. He took Zhong and Xue to the police station for interrogation. Police Chief Wu interrogated them briefly. Considering that the case involved a daylight robbery, he feared there was more to the story and sent Zhong Yuehua and driver Xue Zhiming to the bureau yesterday afternoon for a thorough investigation.

Four British Soldiers Cause an Accident While Driving 110

Car Crashes into a Light Pole, Engine Catches Fire

Three Seriously Injured, One Unharmed

According to the Continental Daily, yesterday afternoon at 4 PM, four British soldiers crashed a service car into a light pole on Daxi Road. All four were seriously injured. As of 1 AM this morning, two of them were still unconscious. The soldier Graydon from the East Lancashire Regiment was in the most critical condition with a ruptured spleen. He is still in the Hong En Hospital this morning and is unlikely to recover. The other three are all military police. One suffered a fractured thigh and is still unconscious. Another suffered a head injury but the injury is less severe. The last one is the least injured, with only skin abrasions. Yesterday afternoon, the four soldiers were all off duty and were traveling west to east on Daxi Road in a Ford car, when they collided with a cement light pole near Hong En Hospital. Due to the force of the impact, the engine caught fire immediately. Fortunately, nearby police officers quickly rescued them and called an ambulance from Hong En Hospital to take them to the hospital. They also reported to the Jing'an Temple Road Fire Department, which sent a fire truck to extinguish the remaining fire in the car and transferred the three military police officers to the British military hospital.

Establishment of the Chinese Archaeological Society 112

Adoption of Constitution and Resolutions

Election of Cai Yuanpei and Others as Directors

The Chinese Archaeological Society held its inaugural meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM in the Mingfu Library of the Science Society of China on Avenue Albert. The meeting adopted the constitution, passed resolutions, and elected directors. Details are as follows:

Attending Members: The attending members included Cai Yuanpei, Yang Quan, Ye Gongchuo, Wang Jiyuan, Liu Haisu, Zhang Feng, Teng Gu, Wei Juxian, Guan Baiyi, Gu Xieyuan, Lu Danlin, Ding Zhonghu, Zheng Shixu, Wang Xiantang, Jin Zutong, Chen Zhiliang, Wu Yichang, Zhang Shuxun, Ma Gongyu, Fang Jiekan, Zheng Zunxiang, Shi Taolu, Gu Dingmei, and Huang Tiren, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, totaling over thirty people.

Chairman's Address: After the meeting commenced, Chairman Cai Yuanpei presided, with Wang Jiyuan as secretary. Following the ceremony, Mr. Cai delivered an address, stating, "The establishment of this archaeological society today may seem like a non-urgent matter. However, human thought has its own strengths, and each should contribute their expertise. Archaeological work can help understand national character and facilitate comparisons with the world. It reveals not only national character but also local characteristics, showcasing local color. Each region has its unique features that we must understand. Antiquities have their temporal context, and every nation has its own era. This applies to humans and animals alike. In the past, communication between nations was inconvenient. Now, other nations admire the culture of the East. Consequently, they use money to buy antiquities. Many of our nation's treasures have been lost overseas. The Japanese say that Chinese people don't need to visit China to see antiquities; they can go to Japan. During the January 28th Incident, the Japanese destroyed our Eastern culture and eradicated traces of our national culture. They are indeed determined to study Eastern culture in Japan. Given this situation, we must strive for self-preservation. England and France repeatedly search for the essence of antiquities for preservation, leaving behind less important items, which will be very dangerous in the future. It is remarkable that we are pursuing this work with archaeological interest and ambition."

Preparatory Process: Next, Huang Tiren, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a speech, followed by Ye Gongchuo, one of the initiators, who reported on the preparatory process, stating, "The reason for establishing this society has been clearly explained by Mr. Cai Zimin. In fact, there is a great need for an archaeological society nationwide, but it has been lacking for many years. Colleagues in Shanghai, aware of this, actively prepared and now announce its establishment. Cultural aggression has been increasing recently, and the impact has also been growing. Moreover, due to internal unrest, antiquities are flowing overseas in greater numbers. Colleagues believe that it is necessary to first improve the situation in Shanghai within possible limits. However, we feel that our strength is weak and our knowledge is shallow, making it difficult to bear this heavy responsibility. Therefore, we invited famous individuals in the country and people with experience and interest in archaeology to a preparatory meeting in March. Initially, the name was set as the Chinese Art and Archaeological Society, but after further discussions, it was changed to the Chinese Archaeological Society because art cannot encompass archaeology, and its nature is different from archaeology. Furthermore, the scope of research is larger. If art is considered archaeology, the meaning cannot be determined. In modern times, archaeology is a specialized science, and there are few researchers in the country. Our society will use archaeology as a basis for archaeological work, hoping that everyone will contribute. We originally planned to hold the meeting in April, but members are scattered throughout the country, and communication takes time, causing the meeting to be delayed until today. Although the number of attendees is not large, most people from Ping, Jin, Hang, Su, Yue, and other regions have not been able to attend but have sent letters urging us to proceed with the work. This is the preparatory process of our society over the past two months."

Adoption of the Constitution: Next was the discussion and adoption of the draft constitution, which was amended and passed. (Chapter 1) Guiding Principles: Article 1: The name of this society is the Chinese Archaeological Society. Article 2: The purpose of this society is to search for archaeological sites and antiquities to promote Chinese culture. Article 3: To achieve the objectives of the preceding article, this society shall successively establish various undertakings. (Chapter 2) Membership: (Individual Members) Article 4: Any person who expresses sympathy for this society and demonstrates achievement in archaeological research or practice, introduced by two or more members of this society and approved by the Board of Directors, may become a member of this society. Article 5: Members of this society must pay membership fees according to the regulations. Those who wish to make special donations are welcome. Article 6: Members have the right to vote and be elected, and may enjoy various facilities and all other benefits provided by this society. (Group Members) Article 7: Any organization related to archaeological research or practice, introduced by two or more members of this society and approved by the Board of Directors, may become a group member of this society. Each group member may designate one person as its representative. Article 8: Group members have the right to enjoy various facilities of this society and the obligation to support the activities of this society. (Chapter 3) Society Affairs: Article 9: The main tasks of this society are as follows: (1) Collecting various archaeological data; (2) Publishing reproductions of antiquities and writings on archaeology; (3) Holding archaeological exhibitions and lectures; (4) Establishing archaeological research institutes and museums; (5) Accepting commissions from the government and public organizations to handle archaeological facilities; (6) Assisting in the preservation of antiquities. Article 10: The tasks mentioned in the preceding article may be implemented gradually according to the circumstances of this society. (Chapter 4) Society Headquarters and Organization: Article 11: The headquarters of this society shall be located in Shanghai. Article 12: This society may establish offices or communication centers in various places at home and abroad when necessary. (A) Board of Directors: (1) Directors: Article 13: This society shall have a Board of Directors composed of seventeen to twenty-one directors. The directors shall elect seven to nine standing directors from among themselves to form the Standing Committee of Directors. Article 14: Directors shall be elected by all members for a term of two years and may be re-elected. (2) Honorary Directors: Article 15: Anyone who has made special contributions to archaeological research or practice or has provided special assistance to this society may be invited to be an honorary director with the approval of the Board of Directors. Article 16: Honorary directors have the right to permanently enjoy the facilities of this society. (3) Staff: Article 17: This society shall have one secretary and several staff members, all of whom shall be appointed by the Board of Directors. Detailed rules for their work shall be formulated separately. (B) Special Committees: Article 18: This society may establish special committees for excavation, investigation, editing, and exhibition with the approval of the Board of Directors when necessary. Their regulations shall be formulated separately. (C) Local Communication Centers: Article 19: Local offices and communication centers shall have one director and several staff members. Their tasks and activities shall be determined by the Board of Directors according to local conditions and implemented through separate regulations. (Chapter 5) Meetings: Article 20: Meetings of this society shall be classified as follows: (1) General membership meeting, held once a year; (2) Regular meeting of the Board of Directors, held once every three months; extraordinary meetings may be convened at any time; (3) Regular meeting of the Standing Committee of Directors, held once a month; extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary; (4) Meetings of special committees shall be conducted according to the regulations of each committee. (Chapter 6) Funding: Article 21: The funding of this society shall be as follows: (1) Membership fee: 5 silver dollars per person; annual membership fee: 5 silver dollars per year; (2) Special donations from members and donations from public and private sources; (3) Income from publications and exhibitions. Article 22: All income of this society shall be used for the society's affairs and shall not be used for other purposes. Article 23: The expenses of local offices and communication centers and their sources shall be determined by the Board of Directors. (Chapter 7) Supplementary Provisions: Article 24: Any imperfections in this chapter may be amended by a resolution of the general membership meeting. Article 25: This chapter shall come into effect on the date of resolution and shall be submitted to the Party and government authorities for record.

Discussion of Proposals: After the amendment and passage of the constitution, proposals were discussed, including: (1) A proposal to edit a quarterly publication based on items 1 and 2 of Article 9 of the constitution; (2) A proposal to determine the location of the society now that it has been established; (3) A proposal to determine the address of the next general meeting; (4) A proposal on whether to hold an archaeological exhibition or lecture after the establishment of the society; (5) A proposal to invite the initiators to make donations first; (6) A proposal that those who responded late to the invitation letters should still be considered initiators. All of the above were resolved to be handled by the Board of Directors.

Election of Directors: Finally, the directors were elected, and the entire body approved the list, which included Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Liu Haisu, Guan Baiyi, Gu Xieguang, Zhang Shuxun, Li Ji, Xie Yingbo, Wang Xiantang, Wang Yiting, Yang Xingfo, Di Pingzi, Wu Hufan, Ma Shuping, Dai Jitao, Li Yinquan, Zhang Congwu, Zhang Tianfang, Dong Kang, and nineteen others. Finally, all members stood up to express their condolences for Mr. Ye Han (Hao Wu), former professor of Peking University, who passed away in Hangzhou. Then, a photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned. It was heard that the first meeting of the Board of Directors would be convened at 7:00 PM last night.

A Youthful Gentleman During the Blind Date, A Crude and Elderly Man at the Wedding 113

A Young Girl from Huzhou Was Shocked and Eloped After Ten Days

Her Biological Mother Was Unreliable, So She Came to Shanghai to Rely on Her Adoptive Mother

The Elderly Groom Came to Shanghai to Search for Her and Filed a Lawsuit

Yang Yueying, a young girl from Huzhou, is twenty-one years old. She has a beautiful figure, a slender build, and is dressed fashionably. Anyone who sees her would consider her a modern woman. After the girl was born to her mother, Yang Shen, due to having too many children and a poor family situation, she was sent to an orphanage before she was even a month old. She was cared for by the orphanage for two years. Suddenly, a woman from the same village, Shi Qian, seeing the girl's bright and lovely complexion, took her home from the orphanage as her adopted daughter.

She was raised and cared for by Ms. Shi, who loved her very much. However, the girl's biological mother, Ms. Shen, lived nearby Ms. Qian. Therefore, she knew all the details of the adoption by Ms. Qian. When the girl reached adulthood and was beautiful and intelligent, her biological mother often saw her on the road and was filled with love and pity. She secretly told the girl about the circumstances of her birth and seduced her in every way. As a result, the girl's intelligence gradually opened, and it was difficult to forget the bond of flesh and blood. At the age of seventeen, she secretly returned to her biological mother's home and moved with her mother to a remote village. Although Ms. Shi Qian sent out scouts everywhere, they could not find her. After a year, her biological mother arranged for her to marry Lin Wenzhang, a fellow villager, as a second wife. However, the girl was quite capricious and insisted on seeing what the groom looked like before agreeing. The matchmaker, seeing the girl's determination, secretly arranged for the girl to go to a certain place to secretly peek at the groom. The girl saw that the groom was a youthful gentleman and agreed immediately. On the engagement day, the Lin family sent four gold ornaments and a gift of 250 silver dollars. In mid-April of last year, the wedding was formally held. The Lin family used drums, flags, and a colorful sedan to welcome her into the home. Who knew that when they entered the bridal chamber and shared the pillow, the girl was about to start whispering sweet words to her youthful groom when she suddenly saw that the groom was crude, dark, and old, with a slight beard on his cheeks. She was shocked. How could he be a completely different person from when she first saw him? The girl was intelligent and wise and decided to temporarily endure since what's done is done and wait to investigate further before making a decision. Her biological mother knew that Lin was over forty years old but only knew that he was marrying her as a second wife. Because she coveted Lin's wealth, she used the trick of substituting one thing for another. Even though her biological mother knew, she played along. After the girl married, within ten days, she learned the truth and found out that Lin's first wife was still alive and was a notorious shrew. If she found out, she would definitely come to punish her. Moreover, she would be living in a secondary room. The girl was both angry and afraid. Therefore, before the honeymoon was over, she seized the opportunity and eloped alone. She didn't want to see her biological mother's face again and had no relatives or friends to rely on. So she took a boat to Shanghai and learned the location of Ms. Shi Qian, her adoptive mother, at 26 Huade Road in Western Shanghai. She went to the address, and after seeing each other, they poured out their hearts and wept together. So, their old feelings were rekindled, and they both went to work in a yarn factory to make a living. Unexpectedly, after a year, the elderly groom, Lin Wenzhang, came to Shanghai to find her and temporarily stayed at 32 Gongyi Lane in Caojiadu in Western Shanghai.

Engaging in Investigation 114

He found out where the girl was. The morning before, Lin found out her address. He went to the address and arrested Yang Yueying and Shi Qian together and took them to the 6th District Police Station. After District Officer Jiang questioned them separately, he determined that the case was related to a marital dispute and was complicated. Therefore, he prepared a document and sent them to the local court for further investigation.

A Man's Body Found Brutally Murdered on Kunshan Road 115

Seemed to Have Fallen from a Height

Reactionary Leaflets Found Near the Body

Yesterday at around 3:50 PM, an unidentified male corpse was suddenly discovered at the back entrance of No. 8 Kunshan Road, North Sichuan Road. The body was wearing a gray rain gauze long gown, a felt hat, and straight Gongni cloth shoes, and appeared to be about 20 years old, resembling a Cantonese. Patrol officers from the Hongkou patrol discovered the body, and upon approaching, they found that the head was bleeding profusely and the person had already died. They immediately took the body to the Tongren Hospital. After examination by the hospital's doctor, it was found that the skull had been broken, and the large intestine was bleeding, suggesting that the person had accidentally fallen from a height, resulting in fatal injuries. A large number of reactionary leaflets and over 50 silver dollars were found in the clothing pocket. The detectives took the items back to the police station for safekeeping and sent detectives to investigate.

Banks on the Bund to Terminate Interest Payments on Silver Accounts 119

Starting June 30th

Due to the abolition of silver, all Chinese and foreign banks on the Bund are now required to convert all current account balances into foreign currency. However, many depositors are unwilling to switch to foreign currency accounts. Therefore, many depositors still maintain accounts in silver. The foreign bank association has now resolved that, starting on June 30th, no interest will be paid on any silver accounts that are still maintained after the deadline. Those who convert their accounts to foreign currency before the deadline will receive interest based on the foreign currency rate. This resolution has been communicated to all banks and depositors for their reference.

Du Laifu Sentenced to Twelve Years for Forcibly Defiling Two Young Girls 120

Du Laifu, a vendor from Ningbo, is 22 years old and makes a living selling rice wine. He lives at the home of his friend Ma Cailin at No. 201 Ziyoufang, Guangdong Road. On the 21st, Ma Fengying suddenly felt severe pain in her lower body and told her mother, Ma Zhang. After questioning her, she told her the truth. She then reported to the Lao Zha Patrol Station, which ordered detectives Huang Yingjie and Bao Tan Wang Rulin to arrest Du. City Sounds 127

Fuan Company Shareholders' Meeting: Yesterday morning at 10 AM, the third shareholders' meeting of the Fuan Company in Xiaodongmen was held on the fourth floor of the company building.
